I looked up sportsbars on my phone and Shooters came up. Despite not having a very positive rating, we decided to stop in for 1 and check it out. I can't tell you how friendly the bartender and the other customers were to us. <Rate>5<//Rate><text>Dr. Lanzon and his staff are excellent - knowledgeable, trustworthy and caring are the three words I would use to describe their services. I would highly recommend Dr. Lanzon for any dental work that you may need.

To give you and idea of what I experienced for my procedure, here is a summary:

My teeth, mostly due to genetics and a love of sugar, were starting to get past the point where they could be saved and rather than keep fixing them one at time for the rest of my life, I made the decision to remove them and replace them with upper and lower implants. This decision was not an easy one but one that was necessary.

With the help of Dr. Lanzon and Dr. Oquist (my dentist), we worked out a treatment and replacement plan that would have the most chance of success. Nothing is guaranteed with this type of major dental work but, after several consultations with Dr. Lanzon, I was confident that he could provide the expertise needed for this "upgrade". And I already knew and trusted that my dentist, who would be coordinating the final appliances (teeth) that would be attached to the implants, was well versed in the process as well. So even though I had no idea what to expect, they did - and their confidence helped to prepare me for what was to come.

First step in the process was to remove my lower teeth, but because I was unsure of how I would react to the removal of my teeth, I decided to just remove half and let the necessary bone grafts become established. In looking back, I should have taken their recommendation to have them all removed at once but to their credit they worked with my two-step plan so that I would feel more comfortable. It turned out that they were right, and that my decision resulted in having to endure one extra healing process (about two months) that could have been avoided had I taken their advice. So the lesson learned here was to accept their advice!!

A few months after this first removal of teeth, I had the remaining lower teeth removed. After pulling the teeth, five implant posts were added. Then a temporary fixed denture was fabricated to fit the posts and attached. All of this was done in a one day session and I was under anesthesia for the entire time so I had no idea what was happening and no pain. When I left his office that day I had new bottom teeth, temporary but impossible to tell that they were not real.

The healing process was brutal for the first few days with lots of rest and enough pain pills to survive. I could not eat normally so it was milk shakes, smoothies, applesauce and mashed potatoes for about a week, and then small sliced up food that could be soft chewed for the next two weeks. After that it was back to normal for food but still staying on the less chewy side of foods so that the healing and strengthening process could continue. Six months later, I had the upper teeth removed, five implant posts were added and then a temporary denture fabricated and attached. Same healing process although the upper implant procedure caused much more swelling than the lower but recovery time was about the same.

Six months after this, we started the process of fabricating the permanent teeth to fit the now sturdy posts. It took a few tweaks to get the teeth just right but once completed they were attached to the posts and have been attached ever since.

Now almost two years after starting the process, I have a perfect set of teeth and a beautiful smile :-)

I am happier, definitely healthier, and all thanks to Dr. Lanzon and Dr. Oquist. I highly recommend them whether you are just doing a small procedure or going for a complete dental replacement. They are well qualified, but more importantly they care about you and your smile. If I had to do it over again, I would choose them and am happy to recommend their services to anyone who is in need of excellent dental care.

B. John</text><Pics>None< /Pics><Resp>None< /Resp><Gmap_id>0x80e83713553007d9:0x98d0d251c29707a8<//Gmap_id></record>

<pics>None</pics>< review>
1st time experiencing acupuncture and didn't quite know what to expect. Definitely an experience I would do again. A lot of the knots, tender spots, and tenseness in my back has improved. Some of the clicking I was experiencing has stopped and is now moving properly. The anxiety and stress has definitely dispersed and my mood has improved as well. Definitely worth a try if you've never experienced it before. They are very accommodating and address the areas your feel are causing problems. I definitely enjoyed it and would highly recommend this place. The are very friendly with good bed side manner.< /review>

< Review>
To be completely honest, I don't know why this place gets such a low rating both on Yelp and Google. It seems like a really popular spot, and everyone was going here, and not the next two spots. Now, as a Canadian I don't fully know what average price for breakfast food is, but since it is an airport, I will say that it is fairly reasonable. I ordered an omelette with sausage inside, with sides of toast, salsa, tater tots, and avocado. And with sour cream as dipping. Again, as a Canadian, I found the portions to be huge, and the price isn't bad(under 15 dollars). The service was nice, too. The lady at the counter walked us through the menu. The food was really good too, and they cook many things fresh.< /Review>

<Rating>4</Rating><text>Impressions from 3 Singaporeans:
- Kaya toast was legit.
- Teh was OK. Not enough tea flavor, but at least it wasn't bitter, which happens if it's over-steeped. Could also taste the condensed milk.
- Nasi lemak: Rice tasted like coconut milk but was also far too sweet. I still enjoyed it though. Sambal and the other ingredients were mostly legit.
- Prata: they put spring onions on it for some reason, which overpowered the flavor of the prata.

< name>
Yan Kuang<//name>
<date>1609560934076<//date><rating>4< /rating>< review>
The Food
If you ever looked for Singaporean food in the bay area, you might realize Killiney Kopitiam is a popular choice. Probably also the closest genuine choice? (Don't get it confused with Kopitiam Cafe in Milpitas though.) I've been there a few times and compared it a bit to my experience in Singapore. Here's also some dishes I've tried
- Yuan Yang (w/Tea & Condense Milk)
- Kaya Toast
- Nasi Lemak
- Laksa
- Char Kway Teow
Most of the selection is pretty good, though I would say they are missing a bit of flare when compared to Singapore. But they still taste good with nice flavors. I would like to go back and try some of their other selection like Bak Kut Teh and Chicken and Rice. Whenever I go to Singapore, I must get Chicken and Rice!

The Miscellaneous
Killiney Kopitiam is on one of the main streets, but there is a decent amount of street parking. They seem to have opened recently, but haven't got a chance to use their inside, cause pandemic. They have takeout or outdoor seating, though your mileage may vary. They have a pretty good selection on their menu, covering most of the Singaporean dishes. Their service is also pretty friendly and sincere.< /review>

<Time>1615666019508</Time><Rate>5< /Rate><userid>109335992756924141039< /userid>< review>
Singaporean food is one of those cuisines that is usually way better in the country of origin. It's got a "little of this, little of that" feel that's tends to result in overdone, overwrought dishes. The solution - bring the country to you! The dishes at Killiney Kopitiam are restrained and delicious.
Just be aware that as soy sauce is to chinese cooking and fish sauce to vietnamese and thai, is shrimp paste to singaporean... It might take a bit of getting used to, but the laksa is addictive once you're there!<//review>

1601959836364<//date>

<Review>I'd say that this the most authentic tasting Singaporean food I've had from a restaurant in the Bay Area thus far. Killiney Kopitiam is a well-loved institution in Singapore, and as a food-crazy Singaporean, I'm so happy (even proud) to see them set up shop here. Mind you, there is no monolithic version of various Singaporean dishes and every restaurant has its own rendition, but I like Killiney's versions in Singapore and here. I seldom write reviews but felt compelled to do this one.

Stepping into the restaurant to place my order brought a tear to my eye, as the place smelt like a proper Singapore food court / Kopitiam (Coffeeshop) with its mixed aromas of Kopi (coffee), teh (tea), toast etc. I ordered several dishes: Roti Prata, Chicken curry, Mee Siam, Mee Rebus, Mee Siam, Seafood Bee Hoon, even iced Teh-C Siew Dai (tea with evaporated milk and less sugar). Tastes just like what I've eaten at the original Killiney Kopitiam(s) in Singapore. Tastes like home.

Mee siam:
Gravy tastes just like what Kiliney's sells, which is a bit in the thicker side of the spectrum of what one can find in Singapore, with more tamarind flavour and less coconut milk. The Bee Hoon (rice vermicelli or Á±≥Á≤â) is a bit thicker but that's consistent with Bee Hoon in general here.  That's mostly just texture anyway, the flavour is great. They even have chives and thin sliced tau kwa, which really completes it.

Mee rebus:
Tastes great, again just like what Killiney sells in Singapore. I prefer my mee rebus with a bit more ground nuts but that's just me. Certainly an authentic mee rebus. Not something I've really ever seen in any other restaurant here. Make sure you finish it with the provided kalamansi limes for max flavour! Could be enhanced even further with a drizzle of Kecap manis (dark sweet soy sauce) and julienned green chillies.

Char Kway Teow:
Pretty good, but somewhat lacking in wok hei (the blend of flavours emerging from the Maillard reaction and smoke as a result of rapid high heat wok cooking). The Kway Teow (thick rice noodles) was rather thicker than what one would typically get in Singapore, but had a good flavour.

Seafood Bee Hoon:
Highly recommended, better than their Char Kway Teow imho. Balance of flavours is good and the chef fried it well with some decent wok hei. Make sure you eat this piping hot for max effect.  Transported me back to a zi char (cooked food) stall in a Singapore Kopitiam.

Chicken curry:
Really good Nyonya style curry, more Singaporean-tasting than any other version I've eaten at any restaurant here. For the less initiated, this is quite different from Thai yellow curry or Jndian curries. I was hoping for a larger portion though, this is essentially an individual-sized portion, essentially one chicken drumstick and potatoes. Tastes just like what Kiliney sells. And it's actually different from curry sauce provided together with the Roti Prata. Killiney in Singapore sells the base sauce in foil packs for home cooks, and they should do so here too! (*hint hint Mr Woon*)

Roti Prata:
Tastes fragrant and light like a Kopitiam roti prata. Shiok and Indo restaurants in Menlo Park and Palo Alto make good roti pratas too, and Indo's may be a bit crispier than the one I got at Killiney. That could be because it was a bit cold by the time I brought Killiney's home. Killiney's also much cheaper than Indo's, $6 vs $9.

Mr Woon, the owner of the Killiney franchise in Singapore, is Hainanese, and the Killiney Kopitiams are typical Hainanese kopitiams. The Hainanese migrants to Singapore established themselves as formidable cooks serving under British colonists, and their cooking is a blend of Chinese, Malay, Indian and Western flavours (just like the melting pot of Singapore). This is reflected in the dishes on offer at Killiney (e.g. chicken curry - blend of Chinese/Malay/Indian, Hainanese pork cutlet - blend of Western/Chinese). Interesting factoid: many of Mr Woon's family members went to Stanford, so there's a Palo Alto connection here.< /Review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN38Q8i4VVjQjRVgnujBjW_UZADq4rRq967E6o=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP2IuudvKbidZuM_PwfS64HeF1uTnsZ4bLBNFo=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNChrl8V4wXijykGUC91coWqQoT2wtZRuwhIX8=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOHMDTjjcCoaqBKtX7II4B29QJE7elEPacbGE4=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNoS19GfDQ26SPXVZRGiD8Rs_Ivkq7JA48v8CU=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNG6pL-edbZ6j4IDj4fG832B8ZEGUWlAQ2DDsU=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pics>< response>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
I've been wanting to check out this kopi tiam ever since they opened up, but only got a chance to do it yesterday. I've been to their original location, and although it's not as good as the ones in Singapore, I think their food and coffee are still pretty good, and definitely satisfy my cravings.

I ordered kaya toast, hainanese chicken rice, and kopi peng (iced coffee with condensed milk). I really enjoyed them all, and the chicken rice is comparable to the one I used to get in Singapore. The coffee was also good, but the kaya toast felt a bit off. I'm not sure how to put it, as it's not bad, but it just doesn't feel the same as the one I usually get.

The food is a bit pricey, but still worth it. When I was working in Singapore, I go to Killiney or other kopi tiam branches almost every day in the morning before work. Safe to say I won't be doing that here, even if it's close to my place.

All in all, it's definitely good enough to satisfy my craving for kopi team, something that the bay area has been missing all this time. I will definitely come back (just not too often).< /text>

< review>
Authentic Singaporean cuisine. Things are spicy enough to have a 'kick'. Nasi lemak and Laksa were both good or Shiok as we would say.

There's about 5 indoor dining tables for 3-5 seats per table on first floor. And another 6 outdoor tables. Amazing authentic food!!!! I haven't had such authentic Singaporean food since leaving the country 15 years ago. The laksa, nasi lemak and chicken rice are all authentic and delicious. In particular the chicken rice has excellent tender juicy chicken that is vastly superior to other Hainanese chicken rice places. The rice is rich and fragrant with chicken oil and the soup is delicious as well. The laksa comes with some exquisite prawns of excellent texture. The broth is decadent and flavorful. The nasi lemak is also competently prepared, with perfect chicken wings and delicious rice.<//Review>

< review>
5 stars for the food/staff and 4 for the wait.
Very good, authentic Singaporean food at reasonable prices for downtown Palo Alto.

Would recommend the nasi lemak and laksa. We wanted to try the bak kut teh and char kway teow but they were out of those dishes by the evening. Get there earlier for lunch if you want to avoid this!

We waited about 40 minutes for our order and the staff seemed really apologetic about the wait. Seems like they are still figuring things out and I hope they can have a system to notify us when our order is ready (text, email), since we wouldn't mind the wait as much if we could walk around downtown.

Will definitely come back and try again when ordering is a bit easier!</review>

< Review>
Update 2018****

My original review was exactly how it was previous to the new manager coming on board. After I posted this review, I received a phone call from Stax Up storage from the new manager Yessenia. And here's my review about the new situation.

Previously I was very disappointed with this storage facility. However, they have new management and the other guy who worked here is gone. I received a call from the manager regarding my review and she was extremely apologetic and asked me if I would come down and speak with her. I agreed and came over and spoke with her. After the meeting I decided to go ahead and get a storage unit here again.

I immediately noticed the change of environment. There is no longer a bunch of homeless, tweekers hanging around, people are not basically living in thier storage anymore and I feel much more comfortable keeping my property here. I felt that they made a huge effort to gain me back as a customer and had made many changes to the facility that are positive.

Plus the girl in the office, Yesenia is awesome! If nothing else , she is a great asset to the company and deserves to get props for the hard work she has invested to turn this property around.

Any issues or questions I have had, have been addressed promptly and professionally.  Now that there has been a positive change in the management, I would recommend the facility to anyone.

One thing I would suggest to Staxup is to please get air conditioning. The summers in EL CAJON are brutal and it's hotter than the halls of HELL.

***Old review from 2014***

My boyfriend rented a unit here without knowing anything about the place. the guy Mike, literally has a bunch of homeless people cleaning units, hanging around all day , sleeping on site in their units or behind the building. Drugs and Tweekers run rampid here. It seems to be the hang out spot. The manager must also be on drugs because there was a lot of sneaky dealings going on. My boyfriend moved out as soon as he could.</Review>

< review>
I love poke places, so I tried here and this is definitely one of these best around. Now a days so many establishments are so similar in taste that you can't really go wrong. But what mainly causes people to come back is the customer service, and this place is a great example of that. While I was ordering, another customer came back on die to an online order confusion and staff helping him (most likely the manager, if not he certainly should be promoted to one) was able to take my order as well as help this other customer fix his order simultaneously while maintaining a great attitude the whole time. I was amazed by his care, customer service, and pride in his work. I really wish I had gotten his name.

And on top of all that, the food was delicious! Definitely can't wait to go back.</review>

‚Ä¢	Came in under estimated repair cost.
‚Ä¢	Many Used Bikes
‚Ä¢	Basic Parts
‚Ä¢	Basic Repairs
‚Ä¢	Offered free adjustment

CONS: This is not a shop set up to service mid to high end bikes. If you‚Äôre a serious cyclist, or aspiring to be, you probably know more than they do and would be better off doing it yourself or going to a higher end shop. I never took the bike back because I lack confidence they can correct there errors.
‚Ä¢	Waves sales tax for good rating (unprofessional, though I took advantage of it at the time)
‚Ä¢	Employees have little to no authority or autonomy, nearly all decisions require deference to Jeremiah.
‚Ä¢	Took Much Longer than time quoted (quoted 1 week, finished in nearly 3)
‚Ä¢	Replaced my tires, which I did not ask them to do, and they made no comment as to why or return my used tires which seemed to me to be in good condition.
‚Ä¢	Asked for a quote to move my shift system from down tube to handlebars. I know this can be done, I have researched it. Rather than admitting he didn't know how to do this, Jeremiah insisted it could not be done and recommended that I add rubber or plastic tubing to the shifter to make them more accessible.
‚Ä¢	Didn‚Äôt replace parts that they quoted they would. (Front Derailer)
‚Ä¢	Replaced my rear 6 gear cartridge with a 7 and apparently was not able to adjust front derailer to clear the additional width so chain grinds against front derailer when in highest gear.
‚Ä¢	Didn‚Äôt return old parts, this make me suspicious.
‚Ä¢	Didn‚Äôt offer or make attempt to fit bike to my height.
‚Ä¢	Incorrectly set brakes, adjusted with the brake release OPEN rather than CLOSED making it impossible to remove the tire without readjusting the brakes.</text>
